if you have the key for\n// the object but not the object itself.\ntype ExplicitKey string\n\n// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc is a convenient default KeyFunc which knows how to make\n// keys for API objects namespace and name\n\t\treturn parts[0], parts[1], nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn \"\", \"\", fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected key format: %q\", key)\n}\n\n// `*cache` implements Indexer in terms of a ThreadSafeStore It is like Indexer but does not\n    28→// (necessarily) know how to extract the Store key from a given\n    29→// object.\n    30→//\n    31→// TL;DR caveats: you must not modify anything returned by Get or List as it will break\n    32→// the indexing feature in addition to not being thread safe.\n    33→//\n    34→// The guarantees of thread safety provided by List/Get are only valid if the caller\n    35→// treats returned items as read-only. For example, a pointer inserted in the store\n    36→// through `Add` will be returned as is by `Get`. Multiple clients might invoke `Get`\n    37→// on the same key and modify the pointer in a non-thread-safe way. Also note that\n    38→// modifying objects stored by the indexers (if any) will *not* automatically lead\n    39→// to a re-index. It is like Indexer but does not\n// (necessarily) know how to extract the Store key from a given\n// object.\n//\n// TL;DR caveats: you must not modify anything returned by Get or List as it will break\n// the indexing feature in addition to not being thread safe.\n//\n// The guarantees of thread safety provided by List/Get are only valid if the caller\n// treats returned items as read-only. For example, a pointer inserted in the store\n// through `Add` will be returned as is by `Get`. Multiple clients might invoke `Get`\n// on the same key and modify the pointer in a non-thread-safe way. Also note that\n// modifying objects stored by the indexers (if any) will *not* automatically lead\n// to a re-index. So it's not a good idea to directly modify the objects returned by\n// Get/List, in general.\ntype ThreadSafeStore interface {\n\tAdd(key string, obj interface{})\n\tUpdate(key string, obj interface{})\n\tDelete(key string)\n\tGet(key string) (item interface{}, exists bool)\n\tList() []interface{}\n\tListKeys() []string\n\tReplace(map[string]interface{}, string)\n\tIndex(indexName string, obj interface{}) ([]interface{}, error)\n\tIndexKeys(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]string, error)\n\tListIndexFuncValues(name string) []string\n\tByIndex(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]interface{}, error)\n\tGetIndexers() Indexers\n\n\t// AddIndexers adds more indexers to this store. deduping is not needed here.\n\t\tstoreKeySet = index[indexedValues[0]]\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Need to de-dupe the return list.\n\t\t// Since multiple keys are allowed, this can happen.\n\t\tstoreKeySet = sets.String{}\n\t\tfor _, indexedValue := range indexedValues {\n\t\t\tfor key := range index[indexedValue] {\n\t\t\t\tstoreKeySet.Insert(key)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn storeKeySet, nil\n}\n\nfunc (i *storeIndex) getKeysByIndex(indexName, indexedValue string) (sets.String, error) {\n\tindexFunc := i.indexers[indexName]\n\tif indexFunc == nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Index with name %s does not exist\", indexName)\n\t}\n\n\tindex := i.indices[indexName]\n\treturn index[indexedValue], nil\n}\n\nfunc (i *storeIndex) getIndexValues(indexName string) []string {\n\tindex := i.indices[indexName]\n\tnames := make([]string, 0, len(index))\n\tfor key := range index {\n\t\tnames = append(names, key)\n\t}\n\treturn names\n}\n\nfunc (i *storeIndex) addIndexers(newIndexers Indexers) error {\n\toldKeys := sets.StringKeySet(i.indexers)\n\tnewKeys := sets.StringKeySet(newIndexers)\n\n\tif oldKeys.HasAny(newKeys.List()...) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"indexer conflict: %v\", oldKeys.Intersection(newKeys))\n\t}\n\n\tfor k, v := range newIndexers {\n\t\ti.indexers[k] = v\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// updateSingleIndex modifies the objects location in the named index:\n// - traces from API server watch events through multiple layers of queueing, processing, and notification dispatch:\\n\\n## 1. ListWatch and Watch Event Reception\\nThe chain begins in `tools/cache/listwatch.go` with the `ListWatch` struct, which wraps `ListFunc` and `WatchFunc` to provide initial list and continuous watch capabilities from the API server. These functions are created via `NewListWatchFromClient()` or `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient()` and implement the `ListerWatcher` interface.\\n\\n## 2. Reflector - Main Event Orchestrator  \\nIn `tools/cache/reflector.go`, the `Reflector` struct acts as the primary coordinator:\\n- `ListAndWatch()` is the main entry point that initiates both list and watch operations\\n- `watch()` method runs the watch loop and calls `handleWatch()` to process incoming events\\n- `handleAnyWatch()` function (lines 782-880) consumes events from the watch stream (`w.ResultChan()`), validates them, and dispatches them to the store via `store.Add()`, `store.Update()`, or `store.Delete()` based on the watch event type (Added, Modified, Deleted, Bookmark)\\n\\n## 3. DeltaFIFO Queue - Delta Accumulation\\nIn `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`, the `DeltaFIFO` struct serves as a queue for accumulated object deltas:\\n- `Add()`, `Update()`, and `Delete()` methods enqueue delta operations (lines 309-340)\\n- These methods call `queueActionLocked()` which creates Delta structs with types: Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, or Replaced\\n- `Pop()` method (lines 576-625) dequeues items and invokes a ProcessFunc with each delta\\n- The Deltas type is a list of Delta objects representing the complete change history for an object\\n\\n## 4. Controller - Reflector and Queue Coordination\\nIn `tools/cache/controller.go`, the `Controller` interface coordinates the pipeline:\\n- `Config` struct specifies the Queue (DeltaFIFO), ListerWatcher, and a ProcessFunc\\n- `controller.Run()` starts the Reflector and a continuous `processLoop()` that pops from the queue\\n- `processLoop()` calls `Queue.Pop()` with a ProcessFunc that executes the configured Process function\\n- `processDeltas()` function (lines 541-573) is the key processor that iterates through deltas and calls the `ResourceEventHandler` methods (OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete), while also updating the cache Store\\n\\n## 5.
